id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Oceanic climate</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png/400px-Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png" width="400" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png/600px-Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png/800px-Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png 2x" data-file-width="4231" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_Cfb_Cfc_Cwb_Cwc.png" class="internal" title="Ampliar"></a></div>World map showing oceanic climate zones <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #66FF33; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Cfb</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #33C701; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Cfc</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #63C764; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Cwb</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #63C764; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Cwc</div> </div></div></div></div>\n<p>An <b>oceanic climate</b>, also known as a <b>marine</b> or <b>maritime</b> climate, is the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen classification</a> of climate typical of west coasts in higher middle latitudes of continents, and generally features cool summers (relative to their latitude) and cool <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winters</a>, with a relatively narrow annual <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a> range and few extremes of temperature, with the exception for transitional areas to <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">continental</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic</a> and highland climates. Oceanic climates are defined as having a monthly mean temperature below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in the warmest month, and above 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) in the coldest month.\n</p><p>It typically lacks a <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> is more evenly dispersed throughout the year.  It is the predominant climate type across much of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> including the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a> region of the United States and Canada, portions of central <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, southeastern <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, southeastern <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> as well as isolated locations elsewhere. Oceanic climates are generally characterised by a narrower annual range of temperatures than in other places at a comparable <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a>, and generally do not have the extremely dry summers of <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climates</a> or the hot summers of <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Oceanic climates are most dominant in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, where they spread much farther inland than in other continents.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Oceanic climates can have considerable storm activity as they are located in the belt of the stormy westerlies. Many oceanic climates have frequent cloudy or overcast conditions due to the near constant storms and lows tracking over or near them. The annual range of temperatures is smaller than typical climates at these latitudes due to the constant stable marine air masses that pass through oceanic climates, which lack both very warm and very cool fronts.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Asia_and_Oceania"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Asia and Oceania</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Indian_Ocean"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">Indian Ocean</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Varieties"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span highland variety (Cwb)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Marine_west_coast_(Cfb)"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Marine west coast Cwc)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Precipitation">Precipitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Precipitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Precipitation in an oceanic climate must have at least 40 millimeters per month. All months must have adequate rain and cloudy conditions are common in oceanic climates. London is an example of an oceanic climate. It experiences reliable and constant precipitation throughout the entire year. Despite this, thunderstorms are quite rare since hot and cold air masses meet infrequently in the region.\nIn most areas with an oceanic climate, precipitation comes in the form of <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rain</a> for the majority of the year. However, some areas with this climate see some <a href="/wiki/Snowfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Snowfall">snowfall</a> annually during winter. Most oceanic climate zones, or at least a part of them, experience at least one snowfall per year. In the poleward locations of the oceanic climate zone ("subpolar oceanic climates," described in greater detail below), snowfall is more frequent and commonplace.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Temperature">Temperature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Temperature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Overall <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a> characteristics of the oceanic climates feature cool temperatures and infrequent extremes of temperature. In the K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification, Oceanic climates have a mean temperature of  0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)) or higher in the coldest month, compared to continental climates where the coldest month has a mean temperature of below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F)). Summers are cool, with the warmest month having a mean temperature below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Poleward of the latter is a zone of the aforementioned <b>subpolar oceanic</b> climate (K\xc3\xb6ppen <i>Cfc</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> with long but relatively mild (for their latitude) winters and cool and short summers (average temperatures of at least 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F) for one to three months). Examples of this climate include parts of coastal <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> and extreme southern <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> (examples include <a href="/wiki/Ushuaia" title="Ushuaia">Ushuaia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas" title="Punta Arenas">Punta Arenas</a>).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Causation">Causation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Causation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Oceanic climates are not necessarily always found in coastal locations on the aforementioned parallels; however, in most cases oceanic climates parallel higher middle latitude oceans. The polar <a href="/wiki/Jet_stream" title="Jet stream">jet stream</a>, which moves in a west to east direction across the middle latitudes, advancing low pressure systems, storms, and fronts. In coastal areas of the higher middle latitudes (45\xe2\x80\x9360\xc2\xb0 latitude), the prevailing onshore flow creates the basic structure of most oceanic climates. Oceanic climates are a product and reflection of the ocean adjacent to them. In the fall, winter, and early spring, when the polar jet stream is most active, the frequent passing of marine weather systems creates the frequent fog, cloudy skies, and light drizzle often associated with oceanic climates. In summer, high pressure often pushes the prevailing westerlies north of many oceanic climates, often creating a drier summer climate (for example in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Northwest coast</a> of <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">America</a>, bathed by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>).\n</p><p>The North Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>, a tropical oceanic current that passes north of the Caribbean and up the East Coast of the United States to <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, then heads east-northeast to the Azores, is thought to greatly modify the climate of Northwest Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> As a result of the Gulf Stream, west-coast areas located in high latitudes like Ireland, the UK, and Norway have much milder winters (for their latitude) than would otherwise be the case. The lowland attributes of western Europe also help drive marine air masses into continental areas, enabling cities such as <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> to have maritime climates in spite of being located well inland from the ocean.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(March 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Oceanic climates in Europe occur mostly in Northwest Europe, from <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> eastward to central Europe. Most of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (away from the Mediterranean), <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, the north coast of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">Cantabria</a>), the western <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, the south of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> and southern portions of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, also have oceanic climates. Examples of oceanic climates are found in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bergen" title="Bergen">Bergen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donostia" class="mw-redirect" title="Donostia">Donostia-San Sebastian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayonne" title="Bayonne">Bayonne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Z\xc3\xbcrich">Z\xc3\xbcrich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skagen" title="Skagen">Skagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. With decreasing distance to the Mediterranean Sea, the oceanic climate of Northwest Europe gradually changes to the subtropical dry-summer or <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> of southern Europe. The line between Oceanic and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">Continental climate</a> in Europe runs in a generally north to south direction. For example, western Germany is more impacted by milder Atlantic air masses than is eastern Germany. Thus, winters across Europe become colder to the east, and (in some locations) summers become hotter. The line between oceanic Europe and Mediterranean Europe normally runs west to east and is related to changes in precipitation patterns and differences to seasonal temperatures.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Americas">The Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">47</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:6.88em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">35</span></div>\n</div></td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0F</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The oceanic climate exists in an arc spreading across the north-western coast of North America from the Alaskan panhandle to northern California, in general the coastal areas of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a>. It includes the western parts of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> panhandle, western portions of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, and north-western <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.  In addition, some east coast areas such as some higher elevations along the southern <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Block_Island" title="Block Island">Block Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">Cape Cod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha&#39;s Vineyard">Martha\'s Vineyard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nantucket,_Massachusetts" class="mw-redirect" title="Nantucket, Massachusetts">Nantucket</a> have a similar climate.<sup id="cite_ref-peel_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The oceanic climate is found in isolated pockets in eastern Mexico.  The White Mountains of Northern Arizona have an oceanic <i>cfb</i> climate. An extensive area of oceanic climates distinguishes the coastal regions of southern <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and extends into bordering <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>. \n</p><p>All mid-latitude oceanic climates are classified as humid. However, some <a href="/wiki/Rainshadow" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainshadow">rainshadow</a> climates feature thermal r\xc3\xa9gimes similar to those of oceanic climates but with <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a>-like (<i>BSk</i>) or even <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>-like (<i>BWk</i>) scarcity of precipitation. Despite the oceanic-like thermal regimes, these areas are generally classified as <a href="/wiki/Steppe_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Steppe climate">steppe</a> or <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert climates</a>. These arid versions of oceanic climates are found in eastern <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Range</a> in the United States, in the <a href="/wiki/Okanagan" title="Okanagan">Okanagan</a> Valley in <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a> in southern <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a> in northern Chile.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The only noteworthy area of Maritime Climate at or near sea-level within Africa is in South Africa from <a href="/wiki/Mossel_Bay,_Western_Cape" class="mw-redirect" title="Mossel Bay, Western Cape">Mossel Bay</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a> coast to <a href="/wiki/Plettenberg_Bay" title="Plettenberg Bay">Plettenberg Bay</a>, with additional pockets of this climate inland of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape" title="Eastern Cape">Eastern Cape</a> and <a href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal" title="KwaZulu-Natal">KwaZulu-Natal</a> coast. It is usually warm most of the year with no pronounced rainy season, but slightly more rain in autumn and spring. The <a href="/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Tristan da Cunha">Tristan da Cunha</a> archipelago in the South Atlantic also has an oceanic climate.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia_and_Oceania">Asia and Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Asia and Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">71</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:9.3em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">57</span></div>\n</div></td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0F</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The oceanic climate is prevalent in the more southerly parts of <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>. A mild maritime climate is in existence in New Zealand. It occurs in a few areas of Australia, namely in the southeast, although average high temperatures during summers there tend to be higher and the summers drier than is typical of subtropical highland climates, with summer maxima sometimes exceeding 40&#160;\xc2\xb0C (104&#160;\xc2\xb0F),<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> and southeastern <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>. It can also be found along the western areas of the south coast of <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> parts with <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a>-like (<i>BSk</i>) or even <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>-like (<i>BWk</i>) scarcity of precipitation.\n</p><p>This climate is found on the Asian mainland in mountainous areas of the tropics, such as the foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=South-west_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South-west China (page does not exist)">south-west China</a>.\n</p><p>The Japanese city of <a href="/wiki/Muroran,_Hokkaido" title="Muroran, Hokkaido">Muroran</a> is the only part of that country with an oceanic climate.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_Ocean">Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Amsterdam" title="\xc3\x8ele Amsterdam">\xc3\x8ele Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Saint-Paul" title="\xc3\x8ele Saint-Paul">\xc3\x8ele Saint-Paul</a>, both part of the <a href="/wiki/French_Southern_and_Antarctic_Lands" title="French Southern and Antarctic Lands">French Southern and Antarctic Lands</a>, are located in the subtropics and have an oceanic climate (akin to Tristan da Cunha; see above).\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0F</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg/250px-Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg/375px-Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg/500px-Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuwara_Eliya_Town_Hall_and_racecourseGround.jpg" class="internal" title="Ampliar"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nuwara_Eliya" title="Nuwara Eliya">Nuwara Eliya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The subtropical highland variety of the oceanic climate exists in elevated portions of the world that are within either the tropics or subtropics, though it is typically found in mountainous locations in some tropical countries. Despite the latitude, the higher altitudes of these regions mean that the climate tends to share characteristics with oceanic climates, though it also tends to experience noticeably drier weather during the lower-sun "winter" season. In locations outside the tropics, other than the drying trend in the winter, subtropical highland climates tend to be essentially identical to an oceanic climate, with mild summers and noticeably cooler winters, plus, in some instances, some snowfall. In the tropics, a subtropical highland climate tends to feature spring-like weather year-round. Temperatures there remain relatively constant throughout the year and snowfall is seldom seen.\n</p><p>Areas with this climate feature monthly averages below 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F) but above \xe2\x88\x923&#160;\xc2\xb0C (27&#160;\xc2\xb0F) (or 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F) using American standards). At least one month\'s average temperature is below 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Without their <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevation</a>, many of these regions would likely feature either <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> climates. These regions are usually designated <i>Cwb</i> (or even <i>Cfb</i> "temperate highland").\n</p><p>This type of climate exists in parts of east, south and southeastern <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>,  interior southern Africa and elevated portions of eastern Africa as far north as <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and of western Africa up to the southwestern <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> highlands also share this climate type. The exposed areas of <a href="/wiki/High_Atlas" title="High Atlas">High Atlas</a>, some mountainous areas across <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">southern Europe</a>, mountainous sections of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and in the highest parts of the states of <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paran\xc3\xa1 (state)">Paran\xc3\xa1</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="S\xc3\xa3o Paulo (state)">S\xc3\xa3o Paulo</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, some mountainous areas across <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, parts of the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Marine_west_coast_.28Cfb.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_west_coast_(Cfb)">Marine west coast (Cfb)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Marine west coast (Cfb)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">59</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:8.36em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">49</span></div>\n</div></td>\n<td><div style="width:1.6em;height:17em;position:relative;padding:0;margin:0">\n<div style="height:0em;bottom:2em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #abc;padding:0;margin:0">&#160;</div>\n<div style="background:#ace;-webkit-print-color-adjust:exact;color-adjust:exact;position:absolute;bottom:2em;left:.2em;width:1.2em;height:2.26em;overflow:hidden">&#160;</div>\n<div style="color:blue;position:absolute;bottom:.5em;left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:70%">4.4</span></div>\n<div style="height:0em;bottom:8em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #cba;padding:0;margin:0">&#160;</div>\n<div style="overflow:hidden;background:#e44;-webkit-print-color-adjust:exact;color-adjust:exact;position:absolute;left:.4em;width:0.8em;bottom:9.28em;height:1.08em;">&#160;</div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:10.36em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">53</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:7.78em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">44</span></div>\n</div></td>\n<td><div style="width:1.6em;height:17em;position:relative;padding:0;margin:0">\n<div style="height:0em;bottom:2em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #abc;padding:0;margin:0">&#160;</div>\n<div style="background:#ace;-webkit-print-color-adjust:exact;color-adjust:exact;position:absolute;bottom:2em;left:.2em;width:1.2em;height:2.38em;overflow:hidden">&#160;</div>\n<div style="color:blue;position:absolute;bottom:.5em;left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:70%">4.7</span></div>\n<div style="height:0em;bottom:8em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #cba;padding:0;margin:0">&#160;</div>\n<div style="overflow:hidden;background:#e44;-webkit-print-color-adjust:exact;color-adjust:exact;position:absolute;left:.4em;width:0.8em;bottom:8.9em;height:1em;">&#160;</div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:9.9em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">49</span></div>\n<div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:7.4em; left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center"><span style="font-size:80%">40</span></div>\n</div></td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0F</td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in inches</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Temperate oceanic climates, also known as "marine mild winter" climates<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> or simply oceanic climates, are found either at <a href="/wiki/Middle_latitudes" title="Middle latitudes">middle latitudes</a> or in tropical areas at higher altitudes. They are often found on or near the west coast of continents; hence another name for Cfb, i.e. "marine west coast" climates. In addition to moderate temperatures year-round, one of the characteristics is the absence of dry season. Except for the western part of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, this type of climate is confined to narrow ranges of occurrences mainly in the low latitudes and to the east of the continents where it appears in the form of "arch" accompanying elevations, as <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It arises in both hemispheres between 35\xc2\xb0 and 60\xc2\xb0: at low altitudes between <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climates</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subartic</a>, although the latter usually are also grouped in marine climates limited by the east border of the ocean basins.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The west winds ease temperatures, even if there is a partial participation of warm <a href="/wiki/Ocean_current" title="Ocean current">sea currents</a>. With the air coming from the ocean predominates the cloudy weather with constant precipitation even in the colder months and the temperature is strongly enlivened. Depending on the continent its distribution is greater due to the absence of <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountains</a> in the north and south direction.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Without a deep layer of snow and sufficient moisture the entire year the <a href="/wiki/Vegetation" title="Vegetation">vegetation</a> is usually always seeing under normal conditions. The vegetation is temperate with the presence of <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">spruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">cedar</a>. As well as <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a>, e.g.: <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">apples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pear" title="Pear">pears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the hottest month the average temperature is below 22 \xc2\xb0 C, but it\'s in minimum four months with temperatures above 10 \xc2\xb0 C. The average temperature of the coldest month must be -3 \xc2\xb0 C or 0 \xc2\xb0 C (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_United_States" title="Eastern United States">eastern United States</a>) to avoid falling into a continental climate in interior areas or of less influence of the adjacent ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The average temperature variations in the year are between 10 and 15 \xc2\xb0 C with average annual temperatures between 7 \xc2\xb0 C and 13 \xc2\xb0 C if it is not a <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountainous</a> place. <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">Rain</a> values can vary from 50 cm to 10 times the minimum value by the <a href="/wiki/Orography" title="Orography">orographic</a> factor. It is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">frontal cyclones</a>, where there are places where rainy days exceed 150 times a year. But contrary to popular belief, there are few <a href="/wiki/Storm" title="Storm">storms</a> and yes they at occurrences of the precipitation are in constant quantities. Another feature is the very reduced visibility in the winter.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1988b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/1988b.jpg/250px-1988b.jpg" width="250" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/1988b.jpg/375px-1988b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/1988b.jpg/500px-1988b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1988b.jpg" class="internal" title="Ampliar"></a></div><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Joaquim" title="S\xc3\xa3o Joaquim">S\xc3\xa3o Joaquim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cfb climates are predominant in central parts of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Green_Spain" title="Green Spain">northern Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, Britain, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. They are the main climate type in  <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australian</a> states of <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> and southeastern <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> (starting from the <a href="/wiki/Illawarra" title="Illawarra">Illawarra</a> region). In North America, they are found mainly in <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a> and neighbouring parts of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, as well as many coastal areas of <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Alaska" title="Southwest Alaska">southwest Alaska</a>. There are pockets of Cfb in most South American countries, including many parts of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Chile" title="Southern Chile">Southern Chile</a>, parts of the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Chubut_Province" title="Chubut Province">Chubut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Province,_Argentina" title="Santa Cruz Province, Argentina">Santa Cruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Province" title="Buenos Aires Province">Buenos Aires</a> in Argentina. In <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> small pockets are found close to sea level on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coast of northern <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>. While Cfb zones are rare in Africa, one dominates the coastline of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape" title="Eastern Cape">Eastern Cape</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.\n</p><p>Rare climates of this subtype include <a href="/wiki/Nantucket" title="Nantucket">Nantucket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> (in the immediate west and northwest in transition for <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental</a>, the remainder of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">Cape Cod</a> <sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and northeastern <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> both in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_United_States" title="Eastern United States">eastern United States</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>, the highest portions of the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">Brazilian state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">Bahia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roraima" title="Roraima">Roraima</a> (in transition or strongly influenced for <i>Cwb</i>), <a href="/wiki/Cuyuni-Mazaruni" title="Cuyuni-Mazaruni">Cuyuni-Mazuruni</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Guianas" title="The Guianas">Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinje,_S%C3%B8r-Tr%C3%B8ndelag" title="Vinje, S\xc3\xb8r-Tr\xc3\xb8ndelag">Vinje</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B8r-Tr%C3%B8ndelag" title="S\xc3\xb8r-Tr\xc3\xb8ndelag">S\xc3\xb8r-Tr\xc3\xb8ndelag</a> in 63.20 \xc2\xb0N (<a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> central coast), <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> (border with <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>), <a href="/wiki/Central_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Central Province, Sri Lanka">Central Province</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, the provinces of <a href="/wiki/B%C3%ACnh_%C4%90%E1%BB%8Bnh_Province" title="B\xc3\xacnh \xc4\x90\xe1\xbb\x8bnh Province">B\xc3\xacnh \xc4\x90\xe1\xbb\x8bnh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qu%E1%BA%A3ng_Ng%C3%A3i" title="Qu\xe1\xba\xa3ng Ng\xc3\xa3i">Qu\xe1\xba\xa3ng Ng\xc3\xa3i</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a> (northeastern <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Balochistan" title="Balochistan">Baluchistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>. Although there are more or less rare places associated with relatively isolated mountainous regions (eg, North <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> islands and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Subpolar_variety_.28Cfc.2C_Cwc.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Subpolar_variety_(Cfc,_Cwc)">Subpolar variety (Cfc, Cwc)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oceanic_climate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Subpolar variety (Cfc, Cwc)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Areas with subpolar oceanic climates feature an oceanic climate but are usually located closer to polar regions. As a result of their location, these regions tend to be on the cool end of oceanic climates. Snowfall tends to be more common here than in other oceanic climates. Subpolar oceanic climates are less prone to temperature extremes than <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climates</a> or <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climates</a>, featuring milder winters than these climates. Subpolar oceanic climates feature only one to three months of average monthly temperatures that are at least 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F). As with oceanic climates, none of its average monthly temperatures fall below -3.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (26.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) or 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C depending on the isotherm used. Typically, these areas in the warmest month experience daytime maximum temperatures below 17&#160;\xc2\xb0C (63&#160;\xc2\xb0F), while the coldest month features highs near or slightly above freezing and lows just below freezing. It typically carries a <i>Cfc</i> designation, though very small areas in <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> have summers sufficiently short to be <i>Cwc</i> with fewer than four months over 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Copacabana,_Bolivia" title="Copacabana, Bolivia">Copacabana, Bolivia</a>, is one the few confirmed towns that features this rare variation of the subpolar oceanic climate. The more warm summer/cool winter variation of this climate type is also sometimes known as a "contimental maritime climate" as it often has more in common with continental climates than with tundra climates, a great example of this would be <a href="/wiki/Harstad" title="Harstad">Harstad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, which like nearby <a href="/wiki/Tromso" class="mw-redirect" title="Tromso">Tromso</a> has moderately cold, snowy winters and mild to warm summers making this somewhat of a cool summer version of a four-season climate. Mountain summits of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">South Island</a> of New Zealand, <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a> of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> expirence the sub polar variety, meaning that they have moderate to cool summers, and snowy winters. \n</p><p>This variant of an oceanic climate is found in parts of coastal <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, small sections of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a>, northwestern coastal areas of <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Lofoten" title="Lofoten">Lofoten</a> and reaching to 70\xc2\xb0N on some islands,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> uplands near the coast of southwestern Norway, the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and northern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Panhandle" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaskan Panhandle">Alaskan Panhandle</a>, the far south of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, and a few highland areas of <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Alps" title="Australian Alps">Australian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Alps_(New_Zealand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Alps (New Zealand)">Southern Alps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This type of climate is even found in the very remote parts of the Papuan Highlands in Indonesia.  The classification used for this regime is Cfc.<sup id="cite_ref-McKnight_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKnight-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In the most marine of those areas affected by this regime, temperatures above 20&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68&#160;\xc2\xb0F) are extreme weather events, even in the midst of summer. Temperatures above 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F) have been recorded on rare occasions in some areas of this climate, and in winter temperatures down to \xe2\x88\x9220&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x924&#160;\xc2\xb0F) have seldom been recorded in some areas.\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em;
